Local News

Principle for Abolishing the Tael and Replacing it with the Yuan is Set 100

Research Association to Meet Tomorrow Afternoon

Chinese and Foreign Banks and Qian Shops Express Agreement

Hu Mengjia and Yu Zuoting Appointed as Representatives

Regarding the issue of abolishing the tael and replacing it with the yuan, since Finance Minister Song Ziwen came to Shanghai and continued discussions with representatives from the local Chinese and foreign banking communities, significant progress has been made. In addition to drafting three principles, a research committee will be jointly established by the government and Chinese and foreign banking communities. It is scheduled to hold its first meeting tomorrow afternoon at 3:00 PM with the representatives appointed by the silver and money industries yesterday to formally study the three principles. Details are as follows:

Three Principles Decided: After arriving in Shanghai last Friday, Song invited banking representatives Bei Songsun, Li Fusun, and foreign banking representatives, totaling several individuals, to his residence at 4:30 PM the following afternoon to continue discussions based on previous progress. Considering the importance of the matter and its complex nature, it was agreed that a thorough discussion was necessary. Therefore, three principles to be discussed were determined: (1) The weight, fineness, and legal tender value of the new silver coin; (2) How to regulate the exchange rate between silver contracts still in effect and silver coins; (3) What methods should be adopted to ensure that the general public understands and trusts this change. It is said that after the above three principles were decided, they were handed over to the research association for abolishing the tael and replacing it with the yuan for discussion.

Establishment of the Research Association: In addition to drafting the above three principles, a research association will be jointly established by the government, Chinese and foreign banking communities, and experts. On the government side, Chen Jianan, Deputy Governor of the Central Bank, will be the chairman. Bei Songsun, General Manager of the Bank of China; Hu Bijiang, General Manager of the China & South Sea Bank; Liu Hongsheng, General Manager of the China Enterprise Bank; and six individuals representing the Western side, including bank representatives and experts Kam, Mazot, and Lynch, will be committee members.

Meeting Scheduled for Tomorrow: After the establishment of the research committee, the first meeting is scheduled to be held tomorrow (Wednesday) at 3:00 PM at the Central Bank. In addition to the participation of Chinese and Western committee members, representatives from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Silver and Money Trade Associations will also be invited. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce has appointed Ma Jiliang, the banking industry has appointed Hu Mengjia, and the money industry has appointed Yu Zuoting to attend the meeting.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Collects Opinions from Various Industries

Regarding the progress of abolishing the tael and replacing it with the yuan, and its future attitude, the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce officially released the following information yesterday through its secretary, Yan E'sheng:

Resolution of the Delegates' Congress: At the meeting of the Third Members' Representative Congress of the Chamber of Commerce, Cai Runsen, the representative of the Fruit and Local Goods Industry, proposed, and Lu Wenshao, the representative of the Rice Trade, and Chen Wenming, the representative of the Medicinal Materials Industry, seconded, a motion urging the government to unify the currency system, abolish the tael and replace it with the yuan as soon as possible, in order to stabilize the financial foundation and benefit commerce. The original text stated: "The government of the Third Year of the Republic (1914) proposed a unified currency system, but it has not been implemented after many years. The reason for the failure to implement it immediately lies in the fact that politics are not on the right track, and provinces govern themselves, resulting in disparate currency systems. The people therefore suffer from this lack of uniformity. The same amount of money, when transferred from Province A to Province B, loses a certain amount in transit. The recent Shanghai war is an example, where the difference in the price of "li" (a small unit of currency) can be as high as five cents per yuan, the harm of which is imaginable. Therefore, we ask the Congress to discuss this matter, which we hope will be realized." After discussion by the Congress, it was resolved to hand over the matter to the Executive Committee to convene the two trade associations of banks and money shops to carefully formulate measures to be submitted to the government for adoption and implementation.

Collecting Opinions from the Two Industries: After the Second Executive Committee was established, the case was brought up for discussion at the first meeting. It was then resolved that, due to the importance of the matter, opinions from the two guilds of silver shops and money shops should be solicited before further processing. Letters were sent to the two guilds on July 2nd. As of yesterday, a reply had been received from the Money Shop Guild, but the Banking Guild had not yet replied as it had just raised the matter for discussion yesterday.

Reply from the Money Shop Guild: The Money Shop Guild's reply to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce stated: "To the esteemed Chamber, abolishing the tael and replacing it with the yuan is one step in reforming the currency system. All Chinese people are happy to see its success. However, this matter is of great importance and requires thorough planning. It is absolutely impossible to proceed with a one-sided mindset. Rather than rushing into things, it may lead to many problems. The benefits may not be seen, but the harm will appear first, causing endless pain to the livelihoods of the people and the national economy. For the sake of caution, our association has prepared humble suggestions and telegraphed them to the Ministry of Finance for adoption and implementation. The text of the telegram has already been disclosed in various newspapers and should be available for inspection. We will not repeat it here. Yesterday, we received a letter from Mr. Chen Jianan of the Central Bank, stating that he had received instructions from the Ministry to organize a committee to study the matter in the long term and to propose three points to be studied. He instructed our association to express our views in writing or by appointing a representative. In addition to appointing a representative to attend the preliminary discussions, we have repeatedly discussed the three points to be studied and sent a detailed reply to Mr. Chen for reference. We believe that this matter is important and is not only related to the silver and money industries, nor is it only related to Shanghai. All industries in the country are closely related to it. Opinions should be collected from all industries first in order to be thorough and avoid obstacles. Your Chamber is the highest commercial organization, and the members are all well-known figures of the time. You must have accurate insights and comprehensive planning on this issue in order to unify the currency system and stabilize society. We are sending a copy of the correspondence with Mr. Chen for your perusal and careful consideration. We look forward to your insights and a unified currency system and the peace of society depend on it."

Wang Xiaolai's Opinion: When the Chamber of Commerce held its third executive committee meeting yesterday, this issue was raised for discussion. The committee members present included Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, Bei Songsun, Yu Zuoting, Luo Qinghua, Lu Wenshao, Ma Jiliang, Chen Zheqing, Fang Jiaobo, Ye Jiaxing, Lao Jingxiu, and Zhu Wenqi. Chairman Wang Xiaolai expressed his opinion that the principle of abolishing the tael and replacing it with the yuan had been passed by the Delegates' Congress and there was no room for discussion. However, detailed discussion of the preparatory measures before and the handling methods after the event was necessary. This matter is by no means just a matter for the silver and money industries, but is related to all industries and the entire society. The issue of grain should be discussed from the standpoint of the people's livelihood and should not be based on the interests of rice shops or restaurants. Currently, various parties have expressed opinions on this issue. I propose that the Chamber of Commerce should wait for the various industries to express their opinions, then summarize them and propose concrete measures.

Appointment of Attending Representative: At the fourth standing committee meeting, the committee had appointed Wang Yansong as the representative to attend the discussion of this issue. Yesterday, Wang stated that he had to go to Qingdao soon to investigate industries and was unable to attend, and requested that another representative be appointed. The executive committee meeting changed the appointment to Ma Jiliang as the attending representative. The Chamber of Commerce then sent a letter to Chen Jianan, President of the Central Bank, to inform him of this change.

Another Research Committee to be Formed: The Chamber of Commerce believes that this matter is of great importance and that it is necessary to solicit opinions from various industries on the three issues inquired about in the letter from Chen Jianan of the Central Bank. It was resolved to send a circular to solicit opinions, and if there are any other opinions besides the three issues, please express them as much as possible. On one hand, the Chamber of Commerce will organize a research committee with seven members. The executive committee has appointed Zhu Wenqi, Fang Jiaobo, Ma Jiliang, Luo Qinghua, Lu Wenshao, Chen Zheqing, and Yi Yunqing as members, and designated Zhu Wenqi as the convener.

Meeting of the Banking Trade Association

The Shanghai Banking Trade Association held an executive committee meeting yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM at the meeting hall at No. 4 Hong Kong Road to discuss the issue of abolishing the tael and replacing it with the yuan. Representatives from various banks were sent to attend the discussion. Details are as follows:

List of Committee Members and Representatives Present: The list of all executive committee members and representatives of various banks is as follows: Li Fusun, Xu Jiqing, Tan Weiwen, Wu Weiru (represented by Wang Zihou), Chen Zheqing, Hu Bijiang, Wu Yunqi (represented by Li Zuji), Tang Baoshu, Xu Boming, Wang Tianshen, Jin Songsheng, Yao Dexin, Liu Hongyuan, Hu Mengjia, Yang Oufu, Xu Xinliu, Xu Weigan, Hu Xiqian, Ye Fuxiao, Bei Songsun, Wang Zhixin, Yu Yuanhui, Wang Boyuan, Xu Baoying, Li Shuxiong, Jing Runshi, and over forty others. Discussion of Various Proposals: Chairman Li Fusun reported on the three principles set by the research association for abolishing the tael and replacing it with the yuan. The committee members and bank representatives then discussed the matter until the meeting adjourned at 3:30 PM. The result was that they all agreed that it was feasible to implement it, and Hu Mengjia was appointed as a representative to participate in the research association for abolishing the tael and replacing it with the yuan.

Money Shops Propose Research Opinions

The Shanghai Money Shop Trade Association specially convened an executive committee meeting to appoint representatives to express their opinions. Details are as follows:

Meeting of the Money Shop Executive Committee: The Money Shop Trade Association held an executive committee meeting at its clubhouse on Ningbo Road the day before yesterday at 2:00 PM. All committee members, including Qin Runqing, Yu Zuoting, Fu Songnian, Pei Yunqing, Hu Xisheng, and Xie Taofu, were present. Chairman Qin Runqing presided over the meeting, and everyone expressed their views on the issue of abolishing the tael and replacing it with the yuan. It was decided to appoint standing committee member Yu Zuoting as the representative to attend the meeting of the research association for abolishing the tael and replacing it with the yuan convened by the Ministry of Finance. After repeated discussion, the three points for which the research committee was seeking opinions were decided upon, and a letter was sent to the research association to submit them.

Money Shop Research Opinions: The Money Shop Trade Association replied to Chen Jianan, Deputy Governor of the Central Bank, yesterday: "Respected Mr. Jianan, regarding the issue of abolishing the tael and replacing it with the yuan, we recently received a letter stating that you were instructed by the Ministry to organize a committee to study the matter in the long term and to propose three points to be studied. You instructed our association to express our views in writing or by appointing a representative to attend the meeting. We have already appointed standing committee member Yu Zuoting as our representative and sent a reply. Now, our association has repeatedly discussed the three points to be studied and proposed the following opinions: (1) The weight and fineness of the new silver coins should, at a minimum, follow the currency system regulations of the Third Year of the Republic (1914) and be actually minted. It is especially necessary to convene various trade groups to form a committee to supervise or assay the coins and publish announcements in newspapers to demonstrate trustworthiness. (2) The conversion of silver taels to silver yuan is not only related to the silver and money industries, nor is it only related to Shanghai. All industries in the country that have creditor-debtor relationships are related. To weigh things fairly, the chambers of commerce in various places should be responsible for convening various industries to discuss and determine them impartially, so as to avoid excessive or insufficient weights and cause obstacles to implementation. (3) To ensure that the general public does not doubt the changes, a unified issuance should be carried out, with a special bureau set up. The reserve fund should be at least 60% in cash, according to law, and should not be offset by other business funds. It is especially necessary to allow various trade groups to have the right to inspect at any time in accordance with the principle of openness, so that the people of the country will not have any doubts and foreigners will have no reason to interfere. This is the most important key to the livelihood of the people and the national economy, and should be given extra attention. The above opinions are for the purpose of reforming the currency system and seeking comprehensive measures, without any bias. The committee members are all well-known figures of the time with rich experience, and there is no need for our association to worry too much. However, since it concerns the national economy and the people's livelihood, we must express our views for contribution. We hope that you will consider them carefully."

Yu Qiaqing Cables Opinions

Leaders from various circles, such as Yu Hede (Yu Qiaqing), have initiated the organization of an economic discussion group to study the pros and cons of abolishing the tael and replacing it with the yuan. It will be formally established in the shortest possible time. Yu believes that abolishing the tael and replacing it with the yuan has a great impact on various industries and that extra caution should be taken beforehand to avoid future troubles. Yesterday, Yu sent telegrams to Chairman Lin of the National Government, Premier Wang of the Executive Yuan, Minister Song of the Ministry of Finance, and Chairman Jiang, stating his opinions. The original telegram to Chairman Jiang is recorded below (the rest are roughly the same, so they are omitted):

Respected Chairman Jiang, I believe that the disorder of currency in our country and its rectification and improvement are indeed important plans. Observing the psychology of all circles in Shanghai, there is unanimous support for the principle of abolishing the tael and replacing it with the yuan. I earnestly hope that it will be realized. However, many people advocate that before implementation, a thorough plan for rectification must be made in order to seek a thorough reform. After the change of the yuan, how should the fineness of the standard currency be determined? How should the old silver coins be disposed of? How should the conversion price between the two yuan be determined? How should the national right of issuance be centralized? And how should the issuance system be improved? All of these must have precise arrangements. Doing it piecemeal will only disturb the market and will not help in practice. Especially since Shanghai is a place where Chinese and foreigners live together and the relationship between creditor and debtor is important, it is even more important to be cautious beforehand. Otherwise, not only will disputes increase, but it will also be chasing after trouble. The consequences are unimaginable. Everything has its advantages and disadvantages. If we only know the cumbersomeness of silver taels without investigating the complexities of silver yuan, and if we only know that silver yuan should be abolished without seeking to reform silver yuan, if we rush forward to achieve success and hastily accomplish things, the results may be unspeakable. Moreover, since the January 28th Incident (1932), Shanghai has been scarred, the market is depressed, unemployment is rampant, and labor unrest is frequent. Without rest and without preparation for this matter, it is reckless to issue an order to abolish the tael and replace it with the yuan. It will inevitably lead to the proliferation of paper money and inferior coins, and the quarrel between creditors and debtors. In the event of a financial turmoil, social instability will be even more dangerous. Jiangsu and Zhejiang are the hometowns of your Excellency, and Shanghai is where the national wealth lies. Moreover, at a time when the work of suppressing the Communists is intense, the security of the rear is important. If there is an incident, the great plan of suppressing the Communists will be abandoned at once, and the collapse of the national economy will follow. I have been in Shanghai for fifty years and have close relationships with all walks of life. What I consider dangerous, I dare not remain silent. I humbly offer my foolishness, and I implore you to consult with the competent authorities and seriously consider this issue. Before there is a thorough solution, do not act rashly, so as to preserve the country's original energy, and the various industries and the country will be fortunate. Yu Hede bows.

Northeast 101

After the Postal Blockade

Universal Postal Union Has Notified All Countries

After our country resolutely blocked the postal service in the East Province, the postal authorities reported the details to the Universal Postal Union. It is now known that the relevant documents have arrived and have been forwarded by the bureau to various countries. Yesterday, Huang Shaoxiong, the acting Minister of Communications, also issued a declaration (see the important telegram column). Details are as follows:

Universal Postal Union Notifies All Countries: Our authorities' resolute blockade of postal services in the East Province was forced by the various oppressions of the Japanese. Therefore, to clarify responsibility, our postal authorities telegraphed the Universal Postal Union in detail, describing the various disturbances caused by the Japanese instigating rebellion, our painstaking efforts to maintain this international postal artery, and the unbearable and unavoidable blockade. We also requested that the postal administrations of the member countries of the Postal Union be notified that from the date of our blockade of postal bureaus in the East Province, mail to Europe or the Americas will not be delivered via Siberia but will be rerouted via the Suez Canal or the Pacific Ocean, and that counterfeit stamps will not be recognized. The message, thousands of words long, was sent on the evening of the 22nd. According to Huang Naishu, Director General of Posts, the telegram has arrived at the secretariat of the Postal Union, and he has received a reply stating that the original telegram has been forwarded to all member countries of the Postal Union.

Ordinary Letters Also Stopped Being Sent Yesterday: The Ministry of Communications ordered the blockade of postal services in the three northeastern provinces on the 23rd. Therefore, starting from the 24th, the local postal bureau has stopped sending registered mail and remittances to the Northeast. Starting yesterday, ordinary letters have also been stopped.

Deputy Postal Director Liu Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Morning: Liu Yaoting, Deputy Postal Director of the Liaoning District, left Shenyang and entered the pass before the blockade. Liu arrived in Beiping some time ago and arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning. He immediately met with Huang Naishu, Director General of Posts, to report on the situation of the Japanese oppression of postal services in the Northeast. Liu intends to work at the General Directorate, but is currently resting due to fatigue from the journey.

First Batch of Postal Workers Transferred Back Enters the Pass: After receiving the Ministry of Communications' order to block postal services in the Northeast, each postal bureau outside the pass began on the 24th. Ba Lidi, Postal Director of Liaoning District, and Smith, Postal Director of Jilin and Heilongjiang District, notified their staff to stop work and ordered all employees to enter the pass in batches. The first batch of more than 500 people entered the pass yesterday and reported to the nearest postal bureau to await instructions. The remaining 1,500 to 1,600 employees will also enter the pass in batches within the next few days.

Huang Naishu Talks About the Blockade Situation: Huang Naishu, Director General of Posts, told the Central News Agency reporter yesterday that the Ministry of Communications ordered the blockade of postal bureaus in the Northeast due to the seizure of postal services in the Northeast. Therefore, all bureaus outside the pass were completely blocked from the 25th of this month. As for the transferred employees, the first batch of more than 500 people entered the pass this morning (i.e., yesterday morning) and reported to the nearest postal bureau. The remaining employees will also be transferred back in batches. As for Ba Lidi, Postal Director of Liaoning District, and Smith, Postal Director of Jilin and Heilongjiang District, etc., they are still outside the pass and the date of entering the pass has not been determined. After the blockade of postal services in the Northeast, all mail to European and American countries, which used to be delivered via Siberia, will now be delivered by sea. Counterfeit stamps issued by the rebels will, of course, be invalid. Postal service is a unified national undertaking and absolutely no disruption from any party is allowed. As for the loss and injury suffered by postal workers in the Northeast, there have been several cases. With sorrow, we have lodged a serious protest with Japan. The only fundamental solution is to quickly recover the lost territory of the Northeast, so that all cases can be solved easily.

Mail to Europe Takes More Time: The North China Daily News reported that the Shanghai Postal Department announced that, due to the postal bureaus in the three eastern provinces being forcibly occupied by the Manchurian puppet government, mail and packages of all kinds to the three eastern provinces have been suspended since July 24. All mail to various parts of Europe, which was originally transported by the Chinese Eastern Railway and the Siberian Railway, has been changed to be transported by sea since July 25. The Dollar Steamship Company's mail ship Madison is scheduled to set sail on the 25th, carrying a large number of mail to Europe, which used to take three weeks to arrive via the Siberian Railway, but now it will take eight or nine days longer. According to Huang Naishu, Director General of Posts, mail to Europe will be transported via Canada or the Suez Canal in the future, using the fastest ships. As for mail from Europe to Shanghai, because postal workers in the three eastern provinces have been ordered to withdraw, European mail that has arrived in Manchuria since July 24 has been stopped from being forwarded. In addition, newspapers from the local area to the three eastern provinces cannot be sent directly by the post office to Shenyang, but if the newspaper has a manager in Dalian, it can be sent to Dalian and forwarded to Shenyang.

Japanese Residents 102

Planning to Establish a Temporary Post Office

Although the Japanese Consulate Has Denied It

Japanese Residents are Still Proceeding

To be Implemented on August 1st

The Far East News Agency reported that Japanese residents in Shanghai, who have been greatly affected by our blockade of postal bureaus in the East Province, held a meeting a few days ago to request the Japanese Consulate to set up a temporary post office dedicated to receiving and sending mail to the East Province for their compatriots. However, according to the Japanese Consulate, this matter is of great importance and it is inconvenient to grant this request from the compatriots. Moreover, postal work is complicated and cannot be handled by setting up a temporary post office. Therefore, it has been rejected. However, according to other sources, although the Japanese Consulate is inconvenient to openly do this due to international relations, Japanese residents are actually actively proceeding with it. It is reported that the Japanese Residents' Association Committee has held several meetings on this issue. Our postal bureau believes that if the Japanese do this, it will violate the spirit of the Universal Postal Union regulations and undermine the integrity of our sovereignty. Therefore, it has ordered the Shanghai Postal Administration to strictly investigate the truth so that it can be reported to the Ministry and forwarded to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to file a protest. The various news are compiled as follows:

Japanese Consulate States: A reporter from the China East News Agency asked Mr. Shirai, the Japanese Deputy Consul stationed in Shanghai, about the attitude of the Japanese residents in Shanghai in organizing a post office. According to Shirai, the Japanese Consulate has no intention of organizing a post office, because postal service is the entire sovereignty of the country and foreigners should not interfere. If a post office is organized, it will conflict with international law. Japanese residents stationed in Shanghai feel inconvenienced because the Chinese authorities have implemented a blockade of postal services in the Northeast, and they may have made this request, but the consulate cannot approve it. As for Japanese residents who entrust ships to transport their private mail to Liaoning, it is their personal action and has nothing to do with the consulate. The reporter also asked what the Japanese side thinks about our country's implementation of the blockade of postal services in the Northeast. According to Shirai, the Japanese government will, of course, protest to the Chinese government about this matter.

Japanese Temporary Post Office: The Shiwen News Agency reported that Japanese residents in Shanghai are planning to set up a temporary post office dedicated to receiving and sending Japanese mail to the Northeast. At 9:00 AM yesterday morning, Lin Xiongji, chairman of the Japanese chambers of commerce in Shanghai, had a two-hour discussion with Japanese Consul Murai. After leaving the Japanese consulate, at 3:00 PM, he issued an emergency notice in the name of the committee, stating that an emergency standing committee meeting would be held at the Japanese Club at 4:00 PM to discuss the date of commencement of the temporary post office and various procedures. All members of the standing committee were present and unanimously decided: (1) Within a month of the trial operation, Japanese residents in Shanghai will be temporarily exempted from sending mail to the Northeast. If the Northeast postal service is still blocked after one month, the previous charging method for mail to the Northeast will still be strictly implemented. (2) The date of commencement of the temporary post office has been decided to be August 1.

Japanese Ships Transport for Free: The Shiwen News Agency reported that the Dalian Steamship Company and Japan Mail Steamship Company have given a very satisfactory answer to the request made by Yasui, the acting administrative committee chairman of the Japanese Residents' Association, to allocate ships to transport Japanese mail to the Northeast. They have also agreed to transport it completely free of charge during the first month of the trial period, and to formulate a plan for subsidies and miscellaneous expenses after one month. The opening date of the ships is every Monday, and each company will allocate a ship for transport. Yasui also gave a very detailed report at the standing committee meeting yesterday afternoon. The Shanghai branches of the Dalian Steamship Company and Japan Mail Steamship Company also sent authorized representatives to attend the meeting to discuss the plan.

Page 14

Parting Words of Ma Kui 103

General Ma's Resolve to Resist Japan to the Death Remains Consistent

If the Nation Has Not Abandoned the Northeast, Please Expedite Assistance

Ma Kui, son of Ma Zhanshan, Chairman of Heilongjiang Province, Ding Shiqiang, son of Ding Chao, Commander-in-Chief of the Jilin Self-Defense Army, Wang Yong, Chief of Staff to Chairman Ma, and Zang Qifang, former Mayor of Tianjin, etc., after coming to Shanghai for discussions, returned north the day before yesterday. A reporter from the New Voice News Agency had the opportunity to meet with young Master Ma and others a few days ago and spoke with them at length. They provided extremely detailed explanations regarding the military and popular sentiment in the Northeast. Following their instructions, the publication was delayed for two days, and it is therefore recorded today. Those concerned about the situation in the Northeast should not regard this as yesterday's news.

Young Master Ma Speaks: According to young Master Ma, his father, around February 27th of this year, acted perforce out of necessity, temporizing with the Japanese. The inner pain at that time was beyond description. Therefore, after arriving in Shenyang, on February 29th, he dispatched a trusted aide disguised as a merchant to enter the customs and report to Director Zhang in Beiping. Because his father was not well-versed in literacy and could not write letters, he only told the aide, "Now I am under the power of the Japanese, like Guan Yu in Cao Cao's camp, my heart is truly with Han. When the opportunity arises, I will rise up again." He also asked him to report to the central government, but still feeling it was not adequate, he dispatched me on March 4th, taking a detour to Europe, and returning to the country by ship from Italy, to report to the central government

and Beiping. When I returned to the country the previous month, I learned that my father had already returned to Heilongjiang Province. However, my father's previous actions had caused suspicion among some people. Now that the truth is out, compatriots across the country have all forgiven him and still expect him to be one who will resist Japan to the end. But what I want to tell compatriots across the country is that my father is completely determined to save the country this time, vowing to fight the Japanese to the death, not succumbing to power, not yielding to profit. Even if he cannot destroy this Rising Sun, he will use all his strength to recover the lost territory, he said.

Military Situation in the Northeast: According to a certain important person who came with Ma, the current situation in the Northeast is as follows: In Heilongjiang Province, the troops currently led by Chairman Ma consist of more than ten brigades, with an estimated 250,000 men. There are also about 80,000 cavalry. Military equipment is quite sufficient, but bullets are needed urgently. In addition, the volunteer army led by Li Haiqing has about 20,000 men, and the militia has 500 to 600 men per regiment, totaling more than 30 counties. In terms of military equipment, there is no need to worry about a shortage of rifles, but what is lacking are heavy artillery and anti-aircraft guns, but the numbers are also not small. The Japanese army is eliminated by these volunteer armies and militias by about 400 to 500 people from time to time. However, the sacrifices of our volunteer army are also quite numerous. Currently, three-tenths of the total area of Heilongjiang Province is in Japanese hands, but all are around the railway, such as the Qiqihar-Keshan Line, the Hulan-Hailun Line, and the Chinese Eastern Railway. They dare not go more than ten miles away from it. As for the regular troops in Jilin Province, there are about 150,000 in total under Ding Chao and Li Du. Many have died in the past battles with the Japanese army. In addition, Gong Changhai, Feng Zhanmei, and the volunteer army Wang Delin and others have more than 35,000 troops, scattered along the eastern border of Jilin. The entire area of Jilin Province, from Dunhua in the south to the northeastern corner of the Songhua River in the north, five-sixths of the area is in the hands of the Japanese, with only one-sixth still within the scope of our army. As for the area along the western section of the Chinese Eastern Railway, the Xinjing-Harbin-Changchun Line, the total number of small volunteer teams is still over 6,000. There are also many with 400 to 500 men in the Changchun and Harbin areas, but because the opportunity has not arrived, ammunition is insufficient, and communication is not established, they are still waiting for orders from the central government to move out. In the Liaoning area, the remaining troops are currently held captive by the Japanese. Only Tang Juwu's troops in eastern Liaoning are under the command of Yu Zhishan, but now, after contacting various parties, there are also 5,000 to 6,000 men. Although they are held captive by the Japanese, if the central government is truly determined to recover the lost territory, they will surely be able to serve the motherland. The volunteer armies in various places in Shenyang also have considerable strength, and are now mostly located east of the South Manchuria Railway and north of Andong. In the Taonan area, Zhang HaiPeng's troops still have 30,000 men, and although they are currently interacting with the Japanese, it is definitely not their true intention. They are all near the Taonan-Changchun Line. In western Liaoning, such as the Yingkou-Goubangzi-Jin County area, there are also more than 100,000 men, now scattered in various places in groups of one or two thousand, but unfortunately lacking a commander. However, they are still confronting the Japanese. These troops do not dare to enter the cities, but the Japanese army does not dare to look at them directly. In southern Liaoning, there are the most militias, with a large portion of about 20,000 men. The remaining large counties and dozens of villages are linked together, and their power cannot be underestimated. Moreover, they have sufficient ammunition and are fighting hard against the Japanese army. The above is just a general situation. What the people of the country should pay attention to now is that if they recognize that the three northeastern provinces are still the whole problem of the Republic of China, they should quickly rise up and provide assistance. Otherwise, with the Japanese scheming and plotting, there will definitely be further aggressive means. What they fear now is our volunteer army. Therefore, they have recently begun to transplant their veterans to the Northeast. This is the first step in preparing to eliminate our volunteer army. If we do not rush to rescue them, the consequences will be unbearable.

Popular Sentiment in General: Continuing, he said, "If the Northeast Incident had occurred thirty years ago, the three northeastern provinces would have long fallen into Japanese hands, with absolutely no room for resistance. This is because the people of the Northeast thirty years ago did not have the intellectual development they have today, and their concept of the nation was extremely superficial. Now, the people of the Northeast have made rapid progress in their knowledge, and their spirit of loving the country and the race is extremely enthusiastic and indignant. Since the incident, in the Rehe area, three or four people have been coming and going every day to make contact, and it is not just one organization. Sometimes it is even rumored that the central government has sent a large army to resist Japan, or that the Beiping army has been dispatched. Although this is close to rumor, their psychology of not forgetting the motherland and eagerly hoping for central government rescue can be seen. To give another example to prove it, when the puppet state was established, celebrations were required everywhere in the Shenyang and Harbin areas. All section members and above had to kneel and kowtow. Each person celebrating held a lamp, but before arriving in Shenyang for the celebration, their lamps were automatically destroyed. This was because they were forced and not voluntary. Even when kneeling and kowtowing, except for a few people on the platform, no one else knelt. In addition, there were many congratulatory slogans posted along the way that day, but the next day they were all torn down by children. If even children are like this, one can imagine the rest. In total, the popular sentiment in the three provinces is somewhat different only near southern Manchuria. The reason is that southern Manchuria has long been under the sphere of Japanese influence, leading to familiarity and lack of awareness. But it is also only a small number, not all. Therefore, I dare to say that although the people of the three northeastern provinces now appear to be dealing with the Japanese, they are only feigning compliance. If there is a complete solution within the customs, all places outside the customs will immediately become armed comrades. Therefore, when recovering the lost territory in the future, this general popular sentiment will definitely provide a great force. Moreover, military victory or defeat is not necessarily about sharp weapons and sufficient ammunition. In ancient times, it was not uncommon for the few to defeat the many. Furthermore, taking the troops of Xi Qia as an example, their soldiers are now under the power of the Japanese army, so they dare not act. If there is a proper solution, they can immediately turn against the Japanese. Taking Xi Qia's previous battle on the Harbin-Changchun Line as an example, when they came into contact with the troops of Ding and Du, they shouted, "How can Chinese people fight their own people?" After shouting, they dispersed in all directions, some defected, some scattered. The previous Battle of Jiangqiao by General Ma was also like this. If these troops had not defected, the Japanese army would not have been so quickly and miserably defeated, although they finally ran out of ammunition and retreated to Hailun. But although this is the action of soldiers, it is also a manifestation of popular sentiment. Therefore, in reality, very few people sincerely submit to the puppet state. Those who do are all those who had conflicts with Zhang Hanqing in the past. Otherwise, the puppet state could never have been established. Currently,

youths of the intellectual class in the three northeastern provinces have returned to Beiping and Tianjin in droves. Those without knowledge, those who can leave have all left, and the rest have joined the volunteer army. Therefore, if there is a solution now, even the university students in the three provinces can immediately call up 3,000 people (there are also 18,000 people who have received military knowledge in the military). These people remain in the Northeast because there is no political solution, and they are all enduring a life of suffering, depression, and indignation. If the central government once has a solution, they are the best vanguard of the people. However, if the government continues to wait and see in the future and still does not adopt a practical method of recovering the territory by force, then this group of young people will definitely have a very serious tragedy. I believe it will be ten times more harmful than the bombs of the Korean people, because they will never be willing to submit to the iron heel of Japanese imperialism. I especially hope that the people of Shanghai will not, because the sound of guns and artillery has moved away from their ears due to the Shanghai War Settlement, neglect the 30 million compatriots in the Northeast who are in deep waters. Whether it is money or ammunition, if it can be continuously supplied, with the strong popular sentiment and arduous struggle in the Northeast, it will definitely not cause the White Mountains and Black Waters to fall under the clogs forever, he said.

Records of the Aviation Association for National Salvation 104

First Review Meeting Held Yesterday

The China Aviation Association for National Salvation held its first review committee meeting at the Bank Association yesterday afternoon at 7:00 PM. Many people including Wang Xiaolai attended, and many important cases were resolved. The details are recorded below.

Attending Committee Members: The review committee members who attended included Wang Xiaolai, Wang Zhengting, Lin Kanghou, Du Yuesheng, Ning Yuanyuan, Lin Wojiang, and many others. Chairman Song Yuanyuan reported on the meeting process and then discussed the revision of the draft and other matters.

Matters Resolved: The matters resolved are as follows: (1) The general association's location will be in Shanghai (2) The first board of directors of the general association will be appointed by the government (3) All citizens of the Republic of China can be members of the association and pay an aviation national salvation fee of one yuan or more per month, which must not be used for other purposes. The rules for collecting money will be set separately (4) The general association's expenses will be allocated by the government, and the provincial branch associations will be allocated by the provincial government. The national salvation fund will be used as an aviation fund, and the membership fee will be borne by the authorities (5) Wang Rutang, Wang Xiaolai, and Lin Kanghou were recommended as members to revise the rules and regulations in principle.

Lin Wojiang Speaks: After the meeting, a reporter from the New Voice News Agency met with Mr. Lin Wojiang. As for the funds for opening, donations will be raised from the public. However, the funds obtained will only be used for aviation. As for the members, they will be allocated by the local authorities. This matter is very hopeful for the future of aviation in our country. Mr. Lin is scheduled to go to Beijing in the next few days.

Manufacturing New Aircraft: During the 19th Route Army's anti-Japanese war, the Aviation Administration received quite a few donations from overseas Chinese. These new aircraft are based on the latest American models. If purchased in the United States, each would cost 150,000 yuan. Now, each costs only slightly less than 100,000 yuan.

Mr. Zeng's Proposal: Zeng Yijing, Director of the Naval Aviation Manufacturing Office, has extremely deep research and experience in aviation science and aviation industry. The effectiveness of the aircraft manufactured by the office itself is no less than that of imported aircraft. However, due to limited funds, Mr. Zeng's ambitions have not been fully realized. Recently, with the establishment of the Aviation Association for National Salvation in Shanghai, Mr. Zeng greatly agrees and plans to have three proposals, all of which are fundamental plans for the development of aviation. The well-known figures in this city, Lin Kanghou, Zhu Boquan, Ye Chunquan, Zhang Naiqi, Chen Xingwei, Shen Shuyu, Yao Yongli, Wu Wenwei, Zhu Zhuanghua, and others, in view of Mr. Zeng's enthusiasm, express their sympathy and specially jointly submit Mr. Zeng's proposals to the Aviation Association for National Salvation, requesting public decision and implementation.

The Bloodstains of the Songhu War Have Not Dried 106

Large Quantities of Japanese Goods Are Being Shipped

"Huashan Maru" Carries Thousands of Tons of Goods

Shipped to North China for Sale Today

Japanese Goods Customs Brokers Are Very Active

After the September 18th Incident, the people of the country rose up to resist Japanese goods. During the January 28th Incident this year, the municipal government surrendered to Japan, and the Japanese army attacked Zhabei that night, causing the war. Trade in Japanese goods in China all stopped. After the Japanese troops withdrew, Japanese merchants urgently sought to restore business with China. However, the boycott movement in the inland was very strong. In the past two months, the import of Japanese goods has been very crowded. Except for a part shipped to various places, the rest are stored in warehouses. Recently, Japanese expatriates in Shanghai are urgently seeking to eliminate our country's boycott of Japanese goods. Today, a large amount of oriental goods began to be loaded to various ports in North China. The details of this matter are investigated and reported as follows.

Negotiations to Stop the Rejection of Goods: Japanese residents in Shanghai, because the Japanese merchants in various places north and south of the Yangtze River who withdrew during the war have now returned to restore pre-war trade. However, because the rejection of goods in the inland is deeply rooted in the hearts of the people, Japanese goods cannot be sold smoothly. The Japanese goods stored in various warehouses in Shanghai amount to tens of thousands of tons. Now they plan to find a way to ship them out. Therefore, a general meeting was specially held to decide to request the Japanese consul in Shanghai to negotiate with our municipal government, requesting our side to fulfill the agreement of January 28th negotiated by Mayor Wu and the Japanese consul, which prohibited Chinese people from boycotting Japanese goods and stopping the rejection of goods movement in various places. They demanded that our government authorities ban it by order. Otherwise, the Japanese side will take further effective coercive measures.

Japanese Goods Piled Up in Various Warehouses: Since the Japanese Post Office resumed the four China-Japan routes, the import of Japanese goods has surged again. Cotton cloth, beer, foreign paper, medicines, leather, toys, etc., are transported in large quantities. The last "Rokka Maru" imported more than 16,000 pieces of Japanese goods. Yesterday, the "Ikomaru" arrived in Shanghai and brought more than 9,700 pieces. As a result, the Japanese goods piled up like mountains in the warehouses of Mitsubishi and HSBC docks. There are still large quantities of oriental goods being continuously loaded to Shanghai.

Large-Scale Exports Today: North China has the most prosperous route for Japanese goods. Recently, since the Dalian Customs blockade occurred, our country must collect import taxes on goods transported to various places in the Northeast through Shanghai. The Japanese side falsely accused us of imposing double customs duties. A large number of Japanese goods in Shanghai are being actively loaded by Japanese merchants to be transferred to North China. Yesterday, the "Huashan Maru" of Nisshin specially moved from Pudong to the Mitsubishi dock to facilitate the loading of huge amounts of Japanese goods onto the ship. The total number is several thousand tons. The "Huashan Maru" is fully loaded. This is the first ship to openly transport large quantities of Japanese goods for export, and it is also the largest batch since September 18th.

Resumption of Japanese Ships on the Yangtze River: For Japanese goods going to the Yangtze River, there have been no ships from the East transporting goods to Shanghai since September last year. Until the 22nd of this month, they finally arrived. Japanese kelp, which had not been imported for ten months, has also begun to be transported. The first batch of Japanese goods to the Yangtze River amounted to more than 700 pieces and has been unloaded at the HSBC and Mitsubishi docks. It is scheduled to be transported to Hankou and other places by Nisshin wheels on the 28th. Japanese wheels on the Yangtze River will also officially resume operations from that day and openly solicit and transport Japanese goods. The Japanese goods customs broker firms organized by Shanghai's traitor merchants Wang and Li have been very active since yesterday, reporting and loading Japanese goods on behalf of others.

Mr. Xu Jiqing Publishes Opinions on Abolishing the Tael and Changing to the Yuan 110

The Legal Tender Should Be Calculated Based on the Silver Content Plus Minting Costs

The Fineness and Weight Should Be Publicly Announced and Subject to Constant Supervision

Paper Money Should Be Subject to Public Inspection by the Issuing Banks

Suspension of Redemption and Centralization of Cash Are Unrelated to Abolishing the Tael

Regarding the issue of abolishing the tael and changing to the yuan, financial leaders and economists have recently expressed many opinions. Recognizing the extreme importance of this matter, a reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency specially visited Mr. Xu Jiqing, a standing committee member of the Bankers Association, yesterday to ask for his views. Mr. Xu has served in the banking industry for more than twenty years, having served as acting governor of the Central Bank and concurrently as director of the mint. His views are highly valued by society. The following is a record of Mr. Xu's formal article to the Xinsheng News Agency titled "An Admonition to Those Who Doubt the Abolition of the Tael and Change to the Yuan."

The matter of abolishing the tael and changing to the yuan has been advocated by us for fifteen years. This is the initial step in reforming the monetary system and is not the end goal. Major aspects such as unifying silver coins, issuing coins, and reorganizing subsidiary coins must all be gradually promoted. After several consultations between the Ministry of Finance authorities and people in the financial industry, it seemed that it could be implemented immediately. Unexpectedly, there are some doubters in the financial industry, and some doubters outside the financial industry, such as economists and lawyers. However, Chinese and foreign merchants unanimously advocate reform. Let us first talk about the benefits of abolishing the tael and changing to the yuan: (1) The financial industry does not need two types of reserves; (2) The public does not have the loss of two types of exchange; (3) When paying customs duties, there is no loss of three types of exchange, converting yuan to tael and tael to customs tael; (4) In international trade, there is no loss of three types of exchange, converting yuan to tael and tael to gold. These are just the major benefits. As reported in various newspapers, people in our financial industry and economists have thoroughly explained the advantages and disadvantages, so there is no need to repeat them. However, looking at the doubters these days, they are not all the same. Generally speaking, there are four major concerns: (1) How to determine the legal tender price; (2) Whether the fineness and weight can be maintained; (3) Whether the issuing banks can avoid excessive issuance; (4) Whether the suspension of redemption and centralization of cash will occur again. Let's first talk about the legal tender price. Every silver yuan should be based on its silver content, and then the actual minting cost should be added to the amount of silver to determine the future legal tender price. This can be proven by numbers. The Ministry of Finance has also stated that it will definitely not seek profits from the mint. This is the first thing that should not be doubted. Next, let's talk about the fineness and weight. The fineness and weight of silver dollars in the future are indeed a cause for concern for us. However, the Nanjing Mint has already been destroyed, and the Hangzhou Mint has also stopped minting. The government will definitely crack down on the remaining mints in various provinces. Assuming that the Central Mint opens minting one day, it will definitely have the effect of unifying coin rights. Once the fineness and weight are determined, they can be announced to the world. It is expected that the matter of public verification can definitely be implemented, and various public groups can also participate and supervise at any time. This is the second thing that should not be doubted. Again, let's talk about whether the issuing banks can avoid excessive issuance. Since the National Government established Nanjing in the sixteenth year of the Republic of China, the Bank of China, fearing the disturbances of the situation, took the lead in advocating the opening of issuance and the establishment of an inspection committee, which inspected twice a month. The committee included one director of the Currency Department, two representatives from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, two representatives from the Shanghai Bankers Association, two representatives from the Shanghai Money Dealers Association, two representatives from the note-receiving banks and money shops, and one accountant. Over the past five or six years, its credit has been particularly prominent. The prescribed 60% cash reserve and 40% security reserve have not been reduced. This can be seen in the announcements in various newspapers. Secondly, banks such as the Central Bank, the Bank of Communications, the Four Banks Joint Treasury, the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, and the China Industrial Bank are inspected monthly by the bank's board of directors and supervisors together with accountants, or by accountants alone. The prescribed 60% cash reserve and 40% security reserve have also not been reduced. This can also be seen in the announcements in various newspapers. In my opinion, those that have been jointly inspected by representatives of various public groups need not be discussed. If those that have not been jointly inspected by representatives of various public groups, the issuing banks can also invite representatives to participate. It is said that a small number of issuing banks that have not been announced can also prepare for public disclosure. The proponents of paper money seem to be alarming. Examining paper money, redemption is the principle. May I ask, without hard currency as a reserve, how can soft currency be issued? This is the third thing that should not be doubted. Again, let's talk about whether the suspension of redemption and centralization of cash will occur again. In the fifth year of the Republic of China, Yuan Shikai proclaimed himself emperor and ordered the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications to suspend redemption. In the sixteenth year of the Republic of China, the Hankou government ordered the centralization of cash. We should not hide the facts of the then government, but these temporary orders were limited to Beijing and Hankou. At that time, Shanghai did not receive the order, so it was not affected. These were all facts before the tael was abolished and the silver yuan was not changed. If we worry that such facts may occur from time to time after the abolition of the tael and the change to the yuan, I dare not believe that it will definitely not happen. Assuming a bad government, regardless of whether the tael has been abolished or not, regardless of whether the silver yuan has been changed or not, if it wants to suspend redemption, it will suspend it. If it wants to centralize cash, it will centralize it. What relationship does this have with the issue of abolishing the tael and changing to the yuan? This is the fourth thing that should not be doubted. I recall that during the May Fourth Movement in the eighth year of the Republic of China, the foreign cent rose to eight qian. Chinese and foreign silver and money dealers jointly planned to cancel the market for British Dragon silver dollars, and British silver dollars gradually disappeared. National currency was able to circulate. Whose power was it? It was the result of the concerted efforts of our financial industry. Now that national currency is already circulating, advancing to abolish the tael will definitely be effective quickly. After the abolition, the reorganization of transfer coins will be started immediately, and the casting of decimal silver and copper subsidiary coins will be prepared. At that time, if there are any further doubts, I will still cite the actual effect of the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications issuing decimal subsidiary coin notes in the past four or five years to inform you. This is truly welcomed by the market, and you all say that there is no need to doubt it. In short, whenever a system is reformed, there will definitely be doubters. Based on what I have known for more than ten years, I will provide an explanation to those who have doubts from all walks of life, and it can also be a reply to reporters who frequently visit. Whether it is a merit or a crime is beyond my knowledge.

Local News 2

Quarantine Dispute over Imported Ships at Shanghai Port Aboard the Xinfeng Steamer 115

Steamer Flying the Flag According to Regulations

Doctor's Delayed Arrival on Board

Police Called to Prohibit Unloading of Goods

Fortunately Resolved Through Mediation

The Shanghai Port Quarantine Office has recently attached great importance to the quarantine of imported merchant ships. All imported ships must not enter the Huangpu River without authorization and must wait for the doctor to examine the passengers before being allowed to enter the port. When each ship arrives in Shanghai, it flies a yellow flag during the day and a three-color red light at night. Yesterday, the China Merchants Bureau's Xinfeng Steamer had a conflict with the Shanghai Port Quarantine Office. The Xinfeng was even prohibited from unloading cargo. It was not until the afternoon that the matter was resolved through negotiations between the two parties. The details of the incident are recorded as follows:

Entering the Port with Flag Flying: The China Merchants Bureau's Xinfeng Steamer, sailing from Tianjin to Shanghai, received a telegram from the head office ordering the ship to proceed to Wusong, where the passengers on board had to be quarantined by the Shanghai Port Quarantine Office. During the day, the ship was ordered to fly the yellow square flag, and the quarantine doctor would arrive. Yesterday morning, the Xinfeng arrived at Wusong and followed the new regulations, hoisting the yellow flag high. The ship moved slowly, but unexpectedly, after sailing into the Wusongkou, no doctor was seen to arrive on board for quarantine. Later, it was learned that the quarantine ship at Wusongkou had been destroyed by the Japanese army and was now being quarantined on the Yangshupu River surface. The Xinfeng then sailed to Yangshupu, but still no doctor arrived. It had no choice but to sail slowly to the Jinliyuan Wharf and docked at 8:40 a.m. By 9 a.m., the doctor had not yet arrived, and the passengers were already causing a commotion on the ship.

Passengers Left Before Doctor Arrived: The Xinfeng had a total of 200 to 300 passengers from Tianjin to Shanghai. When the ship arrived at the wharf, the passengers rushed ashore. The crew could not stop them and had to let the passengers leave the ship. By 9:30 a.m., all the passengers on the ship had disembarked, leaving no one on board. At this time, the medical officer from the Shanghai Port Quarantine Office arrived late. Upon arriving on board and seeing no passengers, he immediately negotiated with the crew. First Mate Jiang Changqing told the doctor that the Xinfeng had been flying the yellow flag since Wusong and entering the port along the river, but no doctor had come for quarantine. It was your office's own negligence, not the ship's evasion. By the time the ship arrived and the passengers left, the crew could not stop them, and the blame was not on the ship.

Prohibition of Unloading: The doctor was furious upon hearing Jiang's words and refused to admit his mistake of being late and derelict in his duties. He immediately went to the shipowner and negotiated with the Xinfeng's shipowner, a foreigner named Crowe, accusing the Xinfeng of violating the Shanghai Port Quarantine Regulations. He then forcibly ordered the ship's engineer to raise the water police flag and summon the water patrol officers. First Mate Jiang Changqing considered this move to be of great importance and stepped forward to stop it, but shipowner Crowe instead ordered the engineer to quickly raise the water police flag. Jiang immediately reported to the bureau. In an instant, the water police arrived on board in response to the call, suspecting that a major incident had occurred on the ship. After the fully armed water police arrived on board, the doctor from the Shanghai Port Office ordered the water police to guard the Xinfeng Steamer and not allow the ship to unload its cargo, thus causing a major dispute.

Mediation Process: The doctor from the Shanghai Port Office prohibited the Xinfeng from unloading, causing panic among the dockworkers and the consignees. They rushed to the bureau to inquire. At the same time, the Shanghai Port Quarantine Office also sent medical officer Chen Yonghan to the China Merchants Bureau to negotiate with Wang Tong, the director of the shipping department. Wang explained to Chen that the Xinfeng had no intention of resisting or violating the quarantine. "After the flag was raised, the doctor did not arrive," and the ship had no way to force the passengers to stay on board. In the afternoon, Wang Tong personally went to the Shanghai Port Quarantine Office and met with Wu Liande, explaining the misunderstanding and requesting that the water police be withdrawn so that the Xinfeng could unload its cargo. It was not until the afternoon that the matter was resolved, and the Xinfeng's cargo was able to be opened and unloaded, but it had been delayed for half a day, causing great concern among the dockworkers and cargo owners.

Water Bill Increases More Than Sevenfold

Various Property Management Offices Send Letters to the Real Estate Association for Negotiation

The Shanghai Real Estate Association received letters yesterday from member companies reporting that the Shanghai Water Company is charging according to the newly installed water meters without obtaining the consent of the homeowners. Jingji Company's Water Bill Increases Threefold: Respectfully, the Shanghai Water Company revised the new contract for water meter billing, and our office refused to sign it and has not recognized it. Unexpectedly, the water company used coercive tactics and acted arbitrarily. Starting from June of this year, it directly calculated according to the water meter reading. Our office received a water bill for June a few days ago, stating that from May 31 to June 25, a total of 25 days, the water consumption was 200,050 gallons, totaling 127.81 yuan, an increase of about three times compared to the original fixed water rate, accounting for 25% of the total house rent. The owner is really unable to bear such an unexpected loss. Now, the total income of the rent for each door number in this neighborhood is listed, and the water bills for January, February, and June of this year are submitted to your association. Please lodge a strong protest with the water company to protect property rights. Sincerely, Shanghai Real Estate Association, Jingji Company, represented by Sun Hezhai.

Qinyu Company's Letter Reporting Water Bill Increase of Sevenfold: Respectfully, our company owns 67 houses in Qinyu Lane, east of Yangshupu Bridge. The total monthly rent is 887 yuan. The water bill for May was 61.85 yuan. Yesterday, we received a water bill from the Shanghai Water Company for June, calculated according to the meter reading for 24 days, totaling 431.81 yuan, which is seven times higher than the May bill. Our company cannot accept it. It is said that the water will be cut off on June 28 if there is no reply. This is a special report to the Shanghai Real Estate Association.

Implementation of the Minimum Standards for Tea in the 21st Year 123

The Commodity Inspection Bureau has Issued Orders to Chinese and Foreign Tea Merchants to Comply

The resolution on the minimum standards for tea inspection in the 21st year of the Second National Commodity Inspection Conference has been stipulated and ordered by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to various commodity inspection bureaus for compliance. After receiving the order, the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau immediately issued a notice and ordered Chinese and foreign tea merchants, Chinese tea warehouses, and foreign merchants reporting for inspection to implement it starting from August 1. The standards are recorded as follows: (Article 1) Green tea shall be based on Ping Shui No. 2 Tea No. 8 Pearl Tea as the standard, red tea shall be based on Hunan Second Red as the standard, and other teas shall be based on clean color, proper fragrance, and good taste as the standard. (Article 2) The moisture content of tea shall be 8.5%, but this year's moisture content for green tea shall be qualified at 9%, red tea shall be qualified at 11%, and other teas shall be qualified at 12%. (Article 3) The maximum ash content of green and red tea shall be 7%, but this year's maximum shall be qualified at 7.5% (Note) 1. The water extract of red tea shall not be less than 26%, and the water extract of green tea shall not be less than 32.2%. 2. The steeped red and green tea shall not exceed 60% (The above two items will be trial standards this year.)
